# Task: Map Test Coverage Gaps in Kafka Consumer Group Coordinator

**Repository:** apache/kafka
**Output:** Write your analysis to `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md`

## Objective

Identify test coverage gaps in Kafka's consumer group coordinator. The group coordinator manages consumer group membership, partition assignment, and offset commits for Kafka consumers.

## Scope

Focus on:
- `core/src/main/scala/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinator.scala` — main coordinator logic
- `core/src/test/scala/unit/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinatorTest.scala` — existing tests
- `core/src/main/scala/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupMetadata.scala` — group state machine

## Content Expectations

Your analysis must:
1. **Identify at least 5 specific failure modes** that are not tested in `GroupCoordinatorTest.scala`
2. **Propose a regression test** for each failure mode (class name, test method signature, key assertions)
3. **Estimate the coverage delta** each proposed test would add (which code paths would it hit)
4. **Label risk level**: HIGH / MEDIUM / LOW

## Output Format

Write to `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md`:

```markdown
# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Kafka Consumer Group Coordinator

## Summary

## Failure Modes and Proposed Tests

### Failure Mode 1: [Name]
- **Risk**: HIGH/MEDIUM/LOW
- **Code Location**: GroupCoordinator.scala ~line NNN
- **Description**: [What failure scenario is untested]
- **Proposed Test**:
  ```java
  @Test
  public void testXxx() { ... }
  ```
- **Coverage Delta**: [Which code paths this test would exercise]

[Repeat for 5+ failure modes]

## File References
```

## Anti-Requirements
- Do not fabricate class or method names — read the actual source first
- Each gap must reference a specific file and approximate location
- Do NOT run the tests yourself — write the test file and the evaluation system validates independently

1262026-03-11T18:45:59.899374agentmessage-
I am thinking...: Interesting! `deleteAllOffsets` iterates `openTransactions.forEachTopicPartition(groupId, ...)` to write tombstones for pending transactional offsets, but it does NOT remove entries from `pendingTransactionalOffsets` (the main map keyed by producerId). 

The `pendingTransactionalOffsets` map is keyed by `producerId` and contains `Offsets` objects that hold the group's pending offsets per producerId. When `deleteAllOffsets` runs, it writes tombstones for the `openTransactions` entries (which track which topic-partitions have open transactions), but the `pendingTransactionalOffsets` map still retains the pending offset data.

Later when `replayEndTransactionMarker(producerId, COMMIT)` fires, it:
1. Removes from `pendingTransactionalOffsets` (so the pending state is removed)
2. For COMMIT: writes to `offsets` map for each pending offset

So if `deleteAllOffsets` was called but didn't remove from `pendingTransactionalOffsets`, then `replayEndTransactionMarker(COMMIT)` could still materialize committed offsets into the `offsets` map for a group that was supposed to be deleted. This is a real bug risk — "ghost" committed offsets re-materializing after group deletion.

This confirms Gap 4 is HIGH risk and very real.

Now let me also check: does `onDeletedTopics` or the replay of tombstones clear `pendingTransactionalOffsets`? Because the sequence in the coordinator is:
1. `deleteAllOffsets` runs (writes tombstones, returns records)
2. Records are appended to log
3. Records are replayed (which runs `replayOffsetCommitTombstone` etc.)
4. Later, `replayEndTransactionMarker(COMMIT)` fires (from Kafka's transaction end marker in the log)

Let me check what `replayOffsetCommitTombstone` does...

1302026-03-11T18:46:38.854735agentmessage-
I am thinking...: This is critical! Looking at `replay()` for tombstones (value == null), lines 1196-1203:

```java
// Remove all the pending offset commits related to the tombstone.
openTransactions.forEach(groupId, topic, partition, openProducerId -> {
    Offsets pendingOffsets = pendingTransactionalOffsets.get(openProducerId);
    if (pendingOffsets != null) {
        pendingOffsets.remove(groupId, topic, partition);
    }
});
openTransactions.clear(groupId, topic, partition);
```

So when offset tombstones are replayed, they DO remove the pending offsets from `pendingTransactionalOffsets`! The logic is:
1. `deleteAllOffsets` writes tombstones for `openTransactions` entries
2. When those tombstones are replayed, `replay()` removes the pending entries from both `pendingTransactionalOffsets` and `openTransactions`

So the pending state IS cleaned up through tombstone replay. This means the "ghost committed offsets" scenario I was concerned about is actually handled correctly (but only after the tombstones are replayed). 

The gap is about the intermediate window between `deleteAllOffsets` being called and its tombstones being replayed. But in the Kafka coordinator model, operations are single-threaded and deterministic — the tombstones from `deleteGroups` are replayed synchronously before any subsequent operations are processed. So there's no concurrent execution issue.

However, there IS still a subtler gap: the scenario where a transactional offset commit arrives AFTER the tombstones are replayed. The sequence could be:
1. Pending transactional offsets are in `pendingTransactionalOffsets` for groupId "foo"
2. `deleteGroups(["foo"])` is called → writes tombstones → tombstones are replayed
3. Tombstone replay removes pending entries from `pendingTransactionalOffsets`

Actually wait - looking more carefully at line 1401:
```java
when(offsetMetadataManager.cleanupExpiredOffsets("other-group-id", List.of())).thenReturn(false);
```

This is a Mockito stub. The argument `List.of()` here is being used as an argument matcher. BUT `List.of()` as a matcher would mean Mockito matches ONLY when the exact `List.of()` immutable list is passed. However, the actual `records` list passed in `cleanupGroupMetadata()` is a mutable `ArrayList`. So this stub might not even match!

### Gap 1 — `cleanupGroupMetadata()`: ClassicGroup full-expiry path · **MEDIUM**

  "thought": "This is critical! Looking at `replay()` for tombstones (value == null), lines 1196-1203:\n\n```java\n// Remove all the pending offset commits related to the tombstone.\nopenTransactions.forEach(groupId, topic, partition, openProducerId -> {\n    Offsets pendingOffsets = pendingTransactionalOffsets.get(openProducerId);\n    if (pendingOffsets != null) {\n        pendingOffsets.remove(groupId, topic, partition);\n    }\n});\nopenTransactions.clear(groupId, topic, partition);\n```\n\nSo when offset tombstones are replayed, they DO remove the pending offsets from `pendingTransactionalOffsets`! The logic is:\n1. `deleteAllOffsets` writes tombstones for `openTransactions` entries\n2. When those tombstones are replayed, `replay()` removes the pending entries from both `pendingTransactionalOffsets` and `openTransactions`\n\nSo the pending state IS cleaned up through tombstone replay. This means the \"ghost committed offsets\" scenario I was concerned about is actually handled correctly (but only after the tombstones are replayed). \n\nThe gap is about the intermediate window between `deleteAllOffsets` being called and its tombstones being replayed. But in the Kafka coordinator model, operations are single-threaded and deterministic \u2014 the tombstones from `deleteGroups` are replayed synchronously before any subsequent operations are processed. So there's no concurrent execution issue.\n\nHowever, there IS still a subtler gap: the scenario where a transactional offset commit arrives AFTER the tombstones are replayed. The sequence could be:\n1. Pending transactional offsets are in `pendingTransactionalOffsets` for groupId \"foo\"\n2. `deleteGroups([\"foo\"])` is called \u2192 writes tombstones \u2192 tombstones are replayed\n3. And `deleteAllOffsets` uses `openTransactions.forEachTopicPartition(groupId, ...)` to find all open transaction topic-partitions. It doesn't simulate the tombstone replay and then call `replayEndTransactionMarker(COMMIT)` to verify the committed offset does NOT re-appear.\n\nActually wait - looking at the code flow:\n1. `deleteAllOffsets` writes tombstone records to `records` list\n2. Those records are returned in `CoordinatorResult`\n3. The runtime appends them to the log\n4. The runtime replays them via `replay()` \n5. producerId) retains its data until tombstones are replayed. Tombstone replay iterates `openTransactions.forEach(...)` to remove per-partition entries from `pendingTransactionalOffsets`, then calls `openTransactions.clear(...)`. If the tombstone replay correctly clears all partitions, the subsequent `replayEndTransactionMarker(COMMIT)` call finds an empty `Offsets` object and commits nothing. If even one partition escapes clearing (e.g., a topic-partition tombstone was not emitted for a pending-only offset because the code guards with `!hasCommittedOffset`), the `pendingTransactionalOffsets` entry for that partition survives and `COMMIT` re-materializes a committed offset for a deleted group.\n\nNo test exercises the full sequence end-to-end.\n\n### Test Evidence\n\n`OffsetMetadataManagerTest`:\n- `testDeleteGroupAllOffsetsWithPendingTransactionalOffsets` (line 2843): calls `deleteAllOffsets` and verifies tombstone records \u2014 stops there.
